# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

{"content":"1: //! The borrowck rules for proving disjointness are applied from the \"root\" of the\n2: //! borrow forwards, iterating over \"similar\" projections in lockstep until\n3: //! we can prove overlap one way or another. Essentially, we treat `Overlap` as\n4: //! a monoid and report a conflict if the product ends up not being `Disjoint`.\n5: //!\n6: //! On each step, if we didn't run out of borrow or place, we know that our elements\n7: //! have the same type, and that they only overlap if they are the identical.\n8: //!\n9: //! For example, if we are comparing these:\n10: //! ```text\n11: //! BORROW:  (*x1[2].y).z.a\n12: //! ACCESS:  (*x1[i].y).w.b\n13: //! ```\n14: //!\n15: //! Because `zip` does potentially bad things to the iterator inside, this loop\n25: //! also handles the case where the access might be a *prefix* of the borrow, e.g.\n26: //!\n27: //! ```text\n28: //! - `mir_borrowck()` in `compiler/rustc_borrowck/src/lib.rs` - The query provider that initiates the entire borrow checking process

- `borrow_conflicts_with_place()` in `compiler/rustc_borrowck/src/places_conflict.rs` - Determines if a borrow place conflicts with an access place
- `places_conflict()` - Public helper function for conflict checking
- Uses sophisticated projection-walking algorithm treating overlap as a monoid

### 3. **Live Range Calculation** 
- `RegionInferenceContext` in `compiler/rustc_borrowck/src/region_infer/mod.rs` - Manages NLL (Non-Lexical Lifetimes) analysis
- `LivenessValues` in `compiler/rustc_borrowck/src/region_infer/values.rs` - Tracks which regions are live at each program point
- `Borrowck` dataflow analysis in `compiler/rustc_borrowck/src/dataflow.rs` - Tracks live borrows during traversal

### 4. **Two-Phase Borrow Resolution**
- `is_active()` in `compiler/rustc_borrowck/src/path_utils.rs` - Uses dominance analysis to determine if a two-phase borrow is in reservation or activation phase
- `check_activations()` in `compiler/rustc_borrowck/src/lib.rs` - Handles borrow activation and conflict checking
- `BorrowSet` and `GatherBorrows` - Collect and track two-phase borrow reservation/activation points

The answer file includes the complete call chain showing how these components integrate to perform comprehensive borrow checking on Rust's MIR.

  "content": "{\"content\":\"1: //! The borrowck rules for proving disjointness are applied from the \\\"root\\\" of the\\n2: //! borrow forwards, iterating over \\\"similar\\\" projections in lockstep until\\n3: //! we can prove overlap one way or another. Essentially, we treat `Overlap` as\\n4: //! a monoid and report a conflict if the product ends up not being `Disjoint`.\\n5: //!\\n6: //! On each step, if we didn't run out of borrow or place, we know that our elements\\n7: //! have the same type, and that they only overlap if they are the identical.\\n8: //!\\n9: //! For example, if we are comparing these:\\n10: //! ```text\\n11: //! BORROW:  (*x1[2].y).z.a\\n12: //! ACCESS:  (*x1[i].y).w.b\\n13: //! ```\\n14: //!\\n15: //! Then our steps are:\\n16: //! ```text\\n17: //!       x1         |   x1          -- places are the same\\n18: //!       x1[2]      |   x1[i]       -- equal or disjoint (disjoint if indexes differ)\\n19: //!       x1[2].y    |   x1[i].y     -- equal or disjoint\\n20: //!      *x1[2].y    |  *x1[i].y     -- equal or disjoint\\n21: //!     (*x1[2].y).z | (*x1[i].y).w  -- we are disjoint and don't need to check more!\\n22: //! ```\\n23: //!\\n24: //! Because `zip` does potentially bad things to the iterator inside, this loop\\n25: //! also handles the case where the access might be a *prefix* of the borrow, e.g.\\n26: //!\\n27: //! ```text\\n28: //! BORROW:  (*x1[2].y).z.a\\n29: //! ACCESS:  x1[i].y\\n30: //! ```\\n31: //!\\n32: //! If this\\n40: //! is a full deep access, then we *know* the borrow conflicts with it. However,\\n41: //! if the access is shallow, then we can proceed:\\n42: //!\\n43: //! ```text\\n44: //!       x1[2].y    | (*x1[i].y)    -- a deref! the access can't get past this, so we\\n45: //!                                     are disjoint\\n46: //! ```\\n47: //!\\n48: //! Our invariant is, that at each step of the iteration:\\n49: //!  - If we didn't run out of access to match, our borrow and access are comparable\\n50: //!    and either equal or disjoint.\\n51: //!  - to influence decisions\\n67: /// where a place might be equal or disjoint with another place, such as if `a[i] == a[j]`.\\n68: /// `PlaceConflictBias::Overlap` would bias toward assuming that `i` borrow_place,\\n92:         BorrowKind::Mut { kind: MutBorrowKind::TwoPhaseBorrow },\\n93:         access_place.as_ref(),\\n94:         AccessDepth::Deep,\\n95:         bias,\\n96:     )\\n97: }\\n98:
